<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Whiston,_Merseyside" title="Whiston, Merseyside">Whiston, Merseyside</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfc_profile2015_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-lfc_profile2015-2">[2]</a></sup> Gerrard started out playing for hometown team Whiston Juniors, where he was noticed by Liverpool scouts. He joined the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" title="Liverpool F.C. Reserves and Academy">Liverpool Academy</a> at age nine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfc_profile_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-lfc_profile-20">[20]</a></sup> He attended <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Heenan_Catholic_High_School" title="Cardinal Heenan Catholic High School">Cardinal Heenan Catholic High School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Gerrard had trials with various clubs at fourteen, but his success wasn't immediate — Gerrard never made it into the England schoolboys' team. Gerrard's trials included <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, which he claimed in his 2006 autobiography was "to pressure Liverpool into giving me a <a href="/wiki/Youth_Training_Scheme" title="Youth Training Scheme">YTS</a> contract."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autobiography_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-autobiography-22">[22]</a></sup> He signed his first professional contract with Liverpool on 5 November 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autobiography_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-autobiography-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings.2C_Cup_treble_and_club_captaincy_.281998.E2.80.932004.29">Beginnings, Cup treble and club captaincy (1998–2004)</span></h4>
<p>Gerrard made his Liverpool first-team debut on 29 November 1998 in a <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> as a last-minute substitute for <a href="/wiki/Vegard_Heggem" title="Vegard Heggem">Vegard Heggem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kay_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kay-23">[23]</a></sup> He made thirteen appearances in his debut season, filling in for injured captain <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Redknapp" title="Jamie Redknapp">Jamie Redknapp</a> in centre-midfield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfc_profile_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-lfc_profile-20">[20]</a></sup> He also occasionally played on the right wing, but he scarcely contributed in the short on-pitch time he received, due to nervousness affecting his play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rich_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rich-24">[24]</a></sup> Gerrard recalled in a November 2008 interview with <i>The Guardian</i>, "I was out of position and out of my depth." The Liverpool hierarchy nonetheless remained convinced that he would improve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rich_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rich-24">[24]</a></sup> Gerrard saw himself as a defensive player primarily, looking to make key tackles rather than push the team forward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kay_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kay-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard began to regularly partner Redknapp in central midfield for the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="1999–2000 Liverpool F.C. season">1999–2000 season</a>. After starting the <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_derby" title="Merseyside derby">derby</a> against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> on the bench, he replaced <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a> in the second half but received his first career <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Misconduct_(football)#Sending-off_offences_.28red_card.29" title="Misconduct (football)">red card</a> for a very late high challenge to the upper leg of Everton's <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Campbell_(footballer)" title="Kevin Campbell (footballer)">Kevin Campbell</a> shortly afterwards in a game Liverpool lost 1-0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Later that season, Gerrard scored his first senior goal in a 4–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> However, he began to suffer from nagging back problems, which sports consultant <a href="/wiki/Hans-Wilhelm_M%C3%BCller-Wohlfahrt" title="Hans-Wilhelm Müller-Wohlfahrt">Hans-Wilhelm Müller-Wohlfahrt</a> later diagnosed as a result of accelerated growth, coupled with excessive playing, during his teenage years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autobiography_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-autobiography-22">[22]</a></sup> He was then beset by groin injuries that required four separate operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autobiography_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-autobiography-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>He went on to recover from this, and in the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2000–01 Liverpool F.C. season">2000–01 season</a> made fifty starts in all competitions and scored ten goals as he won his first major honours with Liverpool – the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_UEFA_Cup" title="2000–01 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>. He was named <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> by his peers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In the following season, he would go on to win both the <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">FA Charity Shield</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a>. In March 2003, Gerrard scored the opening goal in the club's 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2003 Football League Cup Final">Football League Cup Final</a> held at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in Cardiff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-report_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-report-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>After a year as Liverpool vice-captain, Gerrard replaced <a href="/wiki/Sami_Hyypi%C3%A4" title="Sami Hyypiä">Sami Hyypiä</a> as Liverpool captain in October 2003, as manager <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Houllier" title="Gérard Houllier">Gérard Houllier</a> said that he recognised Gerrard had demonstrated leadership qualities early on, but needed to mature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> He chose to extend his contract at the club, signing a new four-year deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Houllier resigned as Liverpool manager after a trophyless <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2003–04 Liverpool F.C. season">2003–04 campaign</a>, and Gerrard was linked with a move to <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> during the off-season. He admitted he was not "happy with the progress Liverpool has made", and that "for the first time in my career I've thought about the possibility of moving on."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In the end, Gerrard turned down a £20 million offer from Chelsea to stay with Liverpool and new coach <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Rafael Benítez">Rafael Benítez</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Chelsea_2008_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Chelsea_2008-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions_League_and_FA_Cup_success_.282004.E2.80.932007.29">Champions League and FA Cup success (2004–2007)</span></h4>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional"></ul>
<p>Liverpool had a number of injuries early in the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2004–05 Liverpool F.C. season">2004–05 season</a>, and a foot injury suffered in a September league match against Manchester United shelved Gerrard until late November. He returned to score in the last five minutes of a Champions League group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiacos</a> to secure Liverpool's advancement to the knockout round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> He claimed that this was his most important, if not his best, goal for Liverpool to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> However, Gerrard netted an own goal during the 2005 <a href="/wiki/2005_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2005 Football League Cup Final">League Cup final</a> on 27 February, which proved decisive in Liverpool's 3–2 loss to Chelsea after extra time at the Millennium Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_big_4-0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_big_4-0.jpg/200px-The_big_4-0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_big_4-0.jpg/300px-The_big_4-0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_big_4-0.jpg/400px-The_big_4-0.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_big_4-0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard playing for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During a six-minute stretch in the second half of the <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">2005 Champions League final</a> against <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a>, Liverpool came back from a three-goal deficit to tie the match at 3–3 after extra time, with Gerrard scoring one of the goals, a header from a John Arne Riise cross.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Liverpool's third goal was gained as a penalty from a foul awarded to Liverpool when <a href="/wiki/Gennaro_Gattuso" title="Gennaro Gattuso">Gennaro Gattuso</a> was judged to have pulled down Gerrard in Milan's penalty box. Xabi Alonso's penalty was saved by Dida but the rebound was scored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Gerrard did not participate in the penalty shootout (he was the designated fifth penalty taker) which Liverpool won 3–2 as they claimed their first Champions League trophy in twenty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Dubbed the <i>Miracle of Istanbul</i>, the match is widely regarded as one of the greatest finals in the competition's history, and Gerrard was lauded as the catalyst for the second half comeback.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Gerrard was named the Man of the Match, and later received the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Club_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="UEFA Club Footballer of the Year">UEFA Club Footballer of the Year</a> award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In regards to his contract issues with Liverpool, Gerrard told the press after the final, "How can I leave after a night like this?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> But negotiations soon stalled and on 5 July 2005, after Liverpool turned down another lucrative offer from Chelsea, Gerrard rejected a club-record £100,000-a-week offer. Liverpool chief executive <a href="/wiki/Rick_Parry" title="Rick Parry">Rick Parry</a> conceded the club had lost Gerrard, saying, "Now we have to move on. We have done our best, but he has made it clear he wants to go and I think it looks pretty final."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The next day, Gerrard signed a new four-year deal as Parry blamed the earlier breakdown of talks on miscommunication between the two sides. Gerrard stated upon signing the contract that he would rather win one premier league medal than win multiple titles at Chelsea as it would mean more to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:28%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Gerrard is for me, in the position he plays, one of the very best in the world. He has a huge impact. For the job he performs, for me, he is one of the greatest."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a> in 2007 with both players named in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFPro_World_XI" title="FIFPro World XI">FIFA World XI</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronaldinho_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ronaldinho-14">[14]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Gerrard scored 23 goals in 53 appearances in <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2005–06 Liverpool F.C. season">2005–06</a>, and in April became the first Liverpool player since <a href="/wiki/John_Barnes_(footballer)" title="John Barnes (footballer)">John Barnes</a> in 1988 to be voted the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Players%27_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Players' Player of the Year">PFA Player of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PFA1_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-PFA1-47">[47]</a></sup> He scored twice in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FA_Cup_Final" title="2006 FA Cup Final">2006 FA Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, including a 35-yard equaliser that sent the match into extra time, and Liverpool won their second consecutive major trophy on penalties. The goals made him the only player to have scored in the FA Cup, League Cup, UEFA Cup and Champions League finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Liverpool eliminated Chelsea in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2006–07 UEFA Champions League">2006–07 Champions League</a> semi-finals on penalties, to return to their second final in three seasons, which they lost 2–1 to Milan in Athens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard suffered a toe fracture in an August 2007 Champions League qualifier against <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_FC" title="Toulouse FC">Toulouse</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> but returned four days later to play the entirety of a 1–1 league draw against Chelsea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> On 28 October 2007, Gerrard played his 400th game for Liverpool in a league match against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>, in which he scored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> He scored in all but one of Liverpool's domestic and European matches during the month of November, and after scoring the only goal in a Champions League away tie against <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Olympique de Marseille</a> on 11 December, he became the first Liverpool player since <a href="/wiki/John_Aldridge" title="John Aldridge">John Aldridge</a> in 1989 to score in seven consecutive games in all competitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In December 2007, Gerrard was voted sixth (after <a href="/wiki/Kak%C3%A1" title="Kaká">Kaká</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a>) for the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_World_Player_of_the_Year" title="2007 FIFA World Player of the Year">2007 FIFA World Player of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_success_and_stardom_.282007.E2.80.932012.29">Continued success and stardom (2007–2012)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg/200px-Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg/300px-Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg/400px-Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gerrard_celebrates_his_second_goal_v_Everton.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard after scoring a hat-trick in the <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_derby" title="Merseyside derby">Merseyside derby</a> in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gerrard made his 300th Premier League appearance on 13 April 2008 in a match against Blackburn Rovers, scoring the opening goal in a game which Liverpool won 3–1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and finished the season with twenty-one goals in all competitions, surpassing his total from the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2006–07 Liverpool F.C. season">2006–07 season</a>. Gerrard was selected for the PFA Team of the Year and he was also one of the nominees or the PFA Player of the Year, alongside teammate <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard needed to undergo groin surgery at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2008–09 Liverpool F.C. season">2008–09 season</a>, but the problem was not serious and he quickly returned to training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> He scored what appeared to be his hundredth career Liverpool goal against <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> on 20 September, but it was disallowed after <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Kuyt" title="Dirk Kuyt">Dirk Kuyt</a> was ruled offside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> He achieved the milestone eleven days later in a 3–1 Champions League group stage win over <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:28%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Is he the best in the world? He might not get the attention of <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Messi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Ronaldo</a> but yes, I think he just might be. He has great passing ability, can tackle and scores goals, but most importantly he gives the players around him confidence and belief. You can't learn that – players like him are just born with that presence."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a> on Gerrard, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zidane_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zidane-65">[65]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>He made his 100th appearance in European club competition for Liverpool on 10 March 2009 against <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> and scored twice in a 4–0 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Four days after the impressive victory over Real, Gerrard would score at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> for the first time from the penalty spot, putting Liverpool ahead on their way to a 4–1 victory over Manchester United.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Following these results, three-time <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Player_of_the_Year" title="FIFA World Player of the Year">FIFA World Player of the Year</a> <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a> hailed the Liverpool skipper as being the best player in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zidane_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zidane-65">[65]</a></sup> On 22 March 2009, Gerrard scored his first ever hat-trick in the Premier League, against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>, in a 5–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 May 2009, Gerrard was named as the 2009 <a href="/wiki/FWA_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="FWA Footballer of the Year">Football Writers' Association Footballer of the Year</a>, beating Ryan Giggs by just 10 votes and becoming the first Liverpool player to win the award in nineteen years. Gerrard was delighted and "a little bit surprised" to win the award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> On 5 December 2009, Gerrard made his 500th appearance for Liverpool in a 0–0 draw at Blackburn where he was accused of <a href="/wiki/Diving_(association_football)" title="Diving (association football)">diving</a> in an attempt to win a penalty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbcdive_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbcdive-70">[70]</a></sup> He ended the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2009–10 Liverpool F.C. season">2009–10 season</a> with a total of 12 goals and nine assists from 46 matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Record-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the 2009–10 season, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Rafael Benítez">Rafael Benítez</a> departed Liverpool after six years and was succeeded as manager by <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a>, who quickly assured fans that Gerrard would not be sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> To further eliminate any speculation surrounding his future at the club, Gerrard made a statement emphasising his excitement at the coming season with Liverpool and praising the signing of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cole" title="Joe Cole">Joe Cole</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Gerrard soon played his first pre-season match of the 2010–11 season against <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> on 1 August 2010 alongside new signing <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cole" title="Joe Cole">Joe Cole</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1017" data-file-width="756" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg/200px-Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg/300px-Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg/400px-Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard before <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a>'s testimonial in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gerrard scored his first goal of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2010–11 Liverpool F.C. season">2010–11 season</a> from the penalty spot in a <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a> qualifier against Macedonian side <a href="/wiki/FK_Rabotni%C4%8Dki" title="FK Rabotnički">FK Rabotnički</a> on 5 August 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> His next two goals came on 19 September at Old Trafford in a 3–2 loss against Manchester United; he scored from a penalty kick in the 64th minute and a free-kick six minutes later to level the game at 2–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> He followed this up one week later with the second equaliser in a 2–2 home draw with <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Eleven days later, Gerrard came off the bench to score a second-half hat-trick in a 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> in the Europa League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard missed the start of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2011–12 Liverpool F.C. season">2011–12 season</a> due to a groin injury, which had also kept him out of action for large parts of the previous season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Gerrard later went on to reveal he rejected the chance to join <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> in the summer to focus on getting Liverpool back in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>, saying "... a traditional club like Liverpool still has a value, that's the reason why I have stuck around for so long ... it is more important to win a couple of trophies and achieve something that is a lot more difficult than go down the easy road and move to a club where it becomes easier."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 October, Gerrard underwent a treatment to clear an infection in his right ankle, which was placed in a protective plaster cast. He was forced to miss Liverpool's league match against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> that day and was ruled out for at least the match against <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> the following week and England's friendly matches against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> the week after that.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> After a prolonged ankle injury recuperation, Gerrard finally returned to regular first team action in the match against <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>, coming off the bench. On 30 December, Gerrard came off the bench against <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> and scored a fine goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard went on to help Liverpool to reach their first cup final in 6 years, and their first at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> in 18 years, as Liverpool beat Manchester City 3–2 on aggregate in the semi-finals. Gerrard scored a penalty in both legs to send Liverpool to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2012 Football League Cup Final">2012 Football League Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> on 26 February 2012, which Liverpool won on penalties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> On his 400th Premier League appearance for Liverpool, Gerrard scored a hat-trick to give Liverpool a 3–0 victory over rivals <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_derby" title="Merseyside derby">Merseyside derby</a> on 13 March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_seasons_with_Liverpool_.282012.E2.80.932015.29">Final seasons with Liverpool (2012–2015)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2073" data-file-width="1349" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg/200px-Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg/300px-Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg/400px-Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_on_his_testimonial.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard during his testimonial in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 18 August 2012, Gerrard played his 250th match as Liverpool captain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> He scored his first Premier League goal of the season on 23 September, opening the scoring in a 2–1 defeat against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 July 2013, Gerrard signed a contract extension with Liverpool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> On 3 August 2013, Liverpool played <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiacos</a>, against whom Gerrard scored arguably his most celebrated goal, at Anfield for Gerrard's charity fund-raising <a href="/wiki/Testimonial_match" title="Testimonial match">testimonial match</a>. Liverpool won the match 2–0, in a game where past players such as <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a> made appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Alder Hey Children's Charity, of which Gerrard is a founding partner, received £500,000 from the proceeds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> On 16 September, Gerrard captained Liverpool for the 400th time in a 2–2 draw at Swansea City. On 5 October, Gerrard scored in a 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>, becoming Liverpool's first ever player to score in 15 successive league campaigns, overtaking the record previously set by <a href="/wiki/Billy_Liddell" title="Billy Liddell">Billy Liddell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Record_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-Record-19">[19]</a></sup> Also in October 2013, Gerrard became the longest-serving Liverpool captain, 10 years after his appointment by Gerard Houllier on 15 October 2013, breaking the previous record held by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Raisbeck" title="Alex Raisbeck">Alex Raisbeck</a>, who captained Liverpool from 1899 to 1909.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On 19 October 2013, Gerrard scored his 100th <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> goal, a penalty against Newcastle United in a 2–2 draw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2106" data-file-width="1458" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg/200px-Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg/300px-Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg/400px-Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_in_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard prior to a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> game in 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 16 March 2014, Gerrard scored two penalties and missed another in Liverpool's 3–0 win over Manchester United at Old Trafford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> On 6 April, he scored another two penalties as Liverpool beat <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> 2–1 to go top of the Premier League table with five matches to play. These goals took him above <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Dalglish" title="Kenny Dalglish">Kenny Dalglish</a> as Liverpool's sixth-<a href="/wiki/List_of_Liverpool_F.C._records_and_statistics#Top_goalscorers" title="List of Liverpool F.C. records and statistics">top goalscorer</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 April, Gerrard was involved in what was later labelled as a defining moment of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14 Premier League</a> season; where Liverpool would ultimately finish second.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GerrardSlip_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-GerrardSlip-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Liverpool originally topped the league when they faced Chelsea in their third last match of the season. Gerrard slipped while receiving a pass which allowed <a href="/wiki/Demba_Ba" title="Demba Ba">Demba Ba</a> to score the opening goal for Chelsea; Chelsea went on to win 2–0, which meant that Liverpool's title hopes were no longer in their own hands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Gerrard finished the season with 13 goals and the League's most assists at 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Gerrard was also a nominee for the PFA Player of the Year award that year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> while he won the 2014 Liverpool Echo Sports Personality Award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Gerrard would later refer to this period as "the worst three months of my life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2014, Gerrard ruled out retiring at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Liverpool F.C. season">2014–15 season</a> and said that he could join another club if he were not offered a new contract at Liverpool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 January 2015, Gerrard announced that he would leave Liverpool at the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Gerrard said he would have signed a new contract had it been offered in the offseason, but said the club did not make an offer until November. By that time, Brendan Rodgers had spoken to him about managing his playing time and he had been left out of the starting lineup against Real Madrid in the Champions League, contributing to his decision to leave Liverpool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 January 2015 Gerrard scored two goals in the 3rd round of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_FA_Cup" title="2014–15 FA Cup">2014–15 FA Cup</a> in a 2–1 win at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A.F.C._Wimbledon" title="A.F.C. Wimbledon">A.F.C. Wimbledon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> This followed another two-goal performance in the previous match against <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester</a>, the first time he scored two or more goals in consecutive games since July 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> On 4 February 2015, he made his 700th appearance for Liverpool, in FA Cup tie against Bolton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 March, Gerrard was sent off 38 seconds after coming on as a half-time substitute in a match against Manchester United for stamping on <a href="/wiki/Ander_Herrera" title="Ander Herrera">Ander Herrera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Gerrard made his 500th league appearance for Liverpool in a goalless draw against West Brom on 25 April; he became only the third player ever to achieve 500 or more Premier League appearances for one club, after <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a> and former teammate <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> His final appearance for Liverpool at Anfield was on 16 May against <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> in a 1–3 loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> His final appearance for the club was eight days later in a 6–1 defeat at Stoke although he scored in the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LA_Galaxy">LA Galaxy</span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Gerrard_announces_retirement_from_professional_football" title="wikinews:Gerrard announces retirement from professional football">Gerrard announces retirement from professional football</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1723" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg/200px-Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg/300px-Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg/400px-Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard playing for <a href="/wiki/LA_Galaxy" title="LA Galaxy">LA Galaxy</a> in 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 7 January 2015, the <a href="/wiki/LA_Galaxy" title="LA Galaxy">LA Galaxy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> announced the signing of Gerrard to an 18-month <a href="/wiki/Designated_Player_Rule" title="Designated Player Rule">Designated Player</a> contract, reportedly worth $9 million. He joined the team in July, following the end of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014–15 Premier League">2014–15 Premier League</a> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 July, Gerrard made his debut for the club in a mid-season friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club América">Club América</a>, playing the first 45 minutes of the match in which Galaxy won 2–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Three days later, Gerrard made his competitive debut for LA, coming on at half time for <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Maganto" title="Ignacio Maganto">Ignacio Maganto</a> in a 1–0 loss at <a href="/wiki/Real_Salt_Lake" title="Real Salt Lake">Real Salt Lake</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">U.S. Open Cup</a> quarter-finals. He made his MLS debut on 17 July, scoring once, while assisting one goal of his former Liverpool teammate <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Keane" title="Robbie Keane">Robbie Keane</a>'s hat-trick, during a 5–2 defeat of fellow Californians the <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Earthquakes" title="San Jose Earthquakes">San Jose Earthquakes</a> at the <a href="/wiki/StubHub_Center" title="StubHub Center">StubHub Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> That month, Gerrard was one of the 22 players to be named to the <a href="/wiki/2015_MLS_All-Star_Game" title="2015 MLS All-Star Game">2015 MLS All-Star Game</a> roster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> He made 13 appearances across the <a href="/wiki/2015_Major_League_Soccer_season" title="2015 Major League Soccer season">regular season</a>, scoring one more goal, the team's last of a 3–2 home win over <a href="/wiki/FC_Dallas" title="FC Dallas">FC Dallas</a> on 27 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> After the Galaxy were eliminated from the <a href="/wiki/2015_MLS_Cup_Playoffs" title="2015 MLS Cup Playoffs">2015 MLS Cup Playoffs</a> by <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle Sounders FC</a>, Gerrard announced that he may retire in 2016, saying that he found unexpected difficulty in the long journeys to away matches in the United States, and the diverse altitude and weather across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard played his final game for Galaxy on 6 November 2016 in a MLS Cup Playoff penalty-shootout loss to <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rapids" title="Colorado Rapids">Colorado Rapids</a>. Gerrard took and scored Los Angeles' first spot-kick but the club were eliminated after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giovanni_dos_Santos" title="Giovanni dos Santos">Giovanni dos Santos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Cole" title="Ashley Cole">Ashley Cole</a> failed to convert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Nine days later, he stated he would be leaving on the expiration of his contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> He then had an interview for the vacant managerial post at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One" title="Football League One">League One</a> club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons" title="Milton Keynes Dons">Milton Keynes Dons</a>, but said that he was not ready for the job.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Gerrard announced his retirement from professional football on 24 November, at age 36.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2017, he was appointed youth coach at Liverpool, effective from February 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<p>Gerrard made his international debut against <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine</a> on 31 May 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> That summer, he was called up for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_European_Football_Championship" title="2000 European Football Championship">Euro 2000</a>, making only one appearance as a substitute in a 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> before England were eliminated in the group stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Gerrard scored his first international goal in the famous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germany_1%E2%80%935_England_(2001)" title="Germany 1–5 England (2001)">5–1 victory over Germany</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 World Cup</a> qualifier in September 2001, and while England qualified, Gerrard was forced to pull out of the squad due to his ongoing groin problems after pulling up in Liverpool's final match of the season against <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard scored his second goal for the national team in the Euro 2004 qualifier against <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_national_football_team" title="Macedonia national football team">Macedonia</a> on 16 October 2002 in a 2–2 draw, his third goal was the opener in a 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Serbia_national_football_team" title="Serbia national football team">Serbia and Montenegro</a> on 3 June 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> He was a regular starter in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a>, scoring once to make it 3–0 in England's win over <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> in the second Group game of the tournament but England would be eliminated by the tournament hosts <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> in the quarter-finals losing 6–5 on penalties in a match when Gerrard was substituted off in the 81st minute for <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hargreaves" title="Owen Hargreaves">Owen Hargreaves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="656" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg/250px-Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg/375px-Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg/500px-Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard_before_Euro_2012_match_vs_Italy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard warming up for <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>He participated in his first <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> in 2006 and scored two goals, both in the group stage, against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinidad_%26_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad &amp; Tobago national football team">Trinidad &amp; Tobago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a>, although his spot kick was one of three saved by goalkeeper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ricardo_Pereira" title="Ricardo Pereira">Ricardo</a> as England again bowed out to Portugal in the quarter-finals on penalties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> He was England's top scorer in the tournament.</p>
<p>Gerrard was made vice-captain of the England team by coach <a href="/wiki/Steve_McClaren" title="Steve McClaren">Steve McClaren</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> and while he filled in for <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a> as captain, England suffered back-to-back losses to <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a> that ended their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2008" title="Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a> qualifying hopes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> After new coach <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Capello" title="Fabio Capello">Fabio Capello</a> took over the team in early 2008, Gerrard was given a trial run as captain but Capello settled on Terry for the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Gerrard was subsequently replaced as England vice-captain by <a href="/wiki/Rio_Ferdinand" title="Rio Ferdinand">Rio Ferdinand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard helped England qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a>, scoring two goals in England's 5–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a> was replaced by Rio Ferdinand as captain in 2010, following revelations about the former's private life,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> and Gerrard subsequently became vice-captain again. When the England team left for the 2010 World Cup, Gerrard was the most experienced player in the squad with 80 caps. During preparations for the 2010 FIFA World Cup, however, Rio Ferdinand was injured, meaning that Gerrard was appointed by Capello as <a href="/wiki/List_of_England_national_football_team_captains" title="List of England national football team captains">captain</a> for the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">[8]</a></sup> After the tournament Gerrard, part of a group of England players dubbed the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_generation#Football" title="Golden generation">Golden Generation</a>", confirmed that he would continue to be available for selection, despite suggestions from Capello that he would seek to re-build the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Captain">Captain</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_(14307138939).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="991" data-file-width="2048" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_%2814307138939%29.jpg/250px-Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_%2814307138939%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_%2814307138939%29.jpg/375px-Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_%2814307138939%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_%2814307138939%29.jpg/500px-Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_%2814307138939%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uruguay_and_England_match_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup_2014-06-19_-_jikatu_(14307138939).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard (second from left) shaking hands with Uruguay's <a href="/wiki/Luis_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Luis Suárez">Luis Suárez</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August 2010, Gerrard scored twice in a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_football_team" title="Hungary national football team">Hungary</a> and helped England to a 2–1 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Due to Ferdinand's continued absence through injury, Gerrard retained the captaincy for the opening match of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying">Euro 2012 qualifying</a> campaign against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulgaria_National_Football_Team" title="Bulgaria National Football Team">Bulgaria</a>, which England won 4–0. He was later named permanent captain by new coach <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a>, in time for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">the tournament finals</a>. This was the first time that he was named directly the captain of England and not in place of an injured or unavailable captain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> He provided three assists and won two man of the match awards to help England finish top of their group in the qualifying round, and go through to the quarter-finals. Despite their exit on penalties to <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>, Gerrard was later the only England player to be named in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Team of the Tournament</a>. On 14 November 2012, Gerrard won his <a href="/wiki/List_of_footballers_with_100_or_more_caps" title="List of footballers with 100 or more caps">100th cap</a> for England in a friendly match against Sweden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, Gerrard captained England to their first group stage elimination since <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958</a> and their first elimination after only two matches, after two straight 1–2 defeats against Italy and Uruguay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Gerrard had played a part in both goals conceded against Uruguay courtesy of his club-mate Luis Suárez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> For England's final game against Costa Rica, Gerrard was replaced as captain by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a> and used as a substitute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 July 2014, Gerrard announced his retirement from international football. He represented England 114 times (currently <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team#Most_capped_players" title="England national football team">the fourth most capped player ever</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Peter_Shilton" title="Peter Shilton">Peter Shilton</a> (125), <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> (117) and <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> (115))<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> scoring 21 times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Henderson" title="Jordan Henderson">Jordan Henderson</a> described Gerrard as "probably the best player this country has ever seen – not only as a player, but also as a leader and a captain."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="482" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg/220px-Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg/330px-Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg/440px-Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_footballer_Steven_Gerrard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard preparing to strike the ball</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A versatile and well-rounded player who is regarded as one of the best midfielders of his generation, Gerrard was capable of playing in a number of positions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> A hardworking <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Box-to-box_midfielder" title="Midfielder">box-to-box</a> player, he was usually deployed as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Central_midfielder" title="Midfielder">central midfielder</a>, but he had also been used as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">second</a> <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Defensive_midfielder" title="Midfielder">holding midfielder</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)#Full-back" title="Defender (association football)">right back</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">right winger</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TEAMtalk_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-TEAMtalk-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Sports_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Sports-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Sports_Review_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Sports_Review-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gerrard began his professional career as a wide midfielder on the right, although he did not excel in this position as he had a tendency to commit careless fouls in his youth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Liverpool retained their faith in the youngster, and he was later shifted to a defensive midfield position as he matured, where he excelled as a ball-winner rather than as a <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thetimes.co.uk_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-thetimes.co.uk-157">[157]</a></sup> He continued to evolve tactically, coming into his own in a box-to-box central midfield role, which allowed him to be effective both offensively and defensively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thetimes.co.uk_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-thetimes.co.uk-157">[157]</a></sup> Under Benítez, he was also used in a supporting and creative role, as an attacking midfielder behind the strikers, or even as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Deep-lying_playmaker" title="Midfielder">deep-lying playmaker</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thetimes.co.uk_157-2"><a href="#cite_note-thetimes.co.uk-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to creating goals, Gerrard, naturally right footed, had the ability to score goals due to his striking ability from distance with both feet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard-159">[159]</a></sup> As he entered his mid 30s and his physical capability to get forward and join the attack declined, the number of long range strikes at goal decreased, with most of his goals coming from free kicks and penalty kicks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Renowned for his pace, work-rate and stamina in his prime, his main attributes in his later career were his vision, ball striking, and his accurate, varied passing range, which allowed him to set the tempo of his team's play and create attacking chances from midfield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> He also possessed good technical and aerial ability, as well as notable defensive attributes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard-159">[159]</a></sup> In particular, Gerrard's tactical intelligence and ability to read the game allowed him to break down the opposition's attacking plays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard_159-3"><a href="#cite_note-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> In addition to his footballing attributes, Gerrard was highly regarded for his leadership, determination, and influence on the pitch throughout his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard_159-4"><a href="#cite_note-Who_is_better:_Scholes_or_Gerrard-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Despite being vocal in his criticism of diving,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Serial_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Serial-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Gerrard was widely accused of diving himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbcdive_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-cbcdive-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Serial_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-Serial-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_football">Outside football</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="600" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Steven_Gerrard.jpg/220px-Steven_Gerrard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Steven_Gerrard.jpg/330px-Steven_Gerrard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Steven_Gerrard.jpg/440px-Steven_Gerrard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Gerrard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gerrard signing autographs in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gerrard was born with <a href="/wiki/Club_foot" title="Club foot">club foot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> He is a practising <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-gm-171">[171]</a></sup> He and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Curran" title="Alex Curran">Alex Curran</a>, married in a Catholic ceremony in Wymondham on 16 June 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-gm-171">[171]</a></sup> He has an older brother, Paul (not to be confused with former Everton goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gerrard" title="Paul Gerrard">Paul Gerrard</a>), and his cousin, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Gerrard" title="Anthony Gerrard">Anthony Gerrard</a>, last played for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_F.C." title="Oldham Athletic F.C.">Oldham Athletic</a>. Steven and Alex have three daughters.</p>
<p>In September 2006, Gerrard published his autobiography, <i>Gerrard: My Autobiography</i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghost_writer" title="Ghost writer">ghost-written</a> by journalist <a href="/wiki/Henry_Winter" title="Henry Winter">Henry Winter</a>, which went on to win the Sports Book of the Year honour at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Book_Awards" title="British Book Awards">British Book Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Gerrard's second volume of autobiography, <i>My Story</i>, written with <a href="/wiki/Donald_McRae_(author)" title="Donald McRae (author)">Donald McRae</a>, was published in September 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gerrard2015_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gerrard2015-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardSep15_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuardSep15-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>The autobiography ends with "I play for Jon-Paul." Gerrard's cousin, Jon-Paul Gilhooley, was killed in the 1989 <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_disaster" title="Hillsborough disaster">Hillsborough disaster</a>, when Gerrard was eight. Jon-Paul, who was 10 when he died, was the youngest of the 96 victims of the tragedy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> "It was difficult knowing one of your cousins had lost his life", Gerrard said. "Seeing his family's reaction drove me on to become the player I am today."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 October 2007, Gerrard was involved in a low-speed collision in <a href="/wiki/Southport" title="Southport">Southport</a> when the car he was driving hit a ten-year-old cyclist, who had shot into the street and inadvertently crossed Gerrard's path. He later visited the boy in the hospital and presented him with a pair of boots signed by <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a>, the boy's favourite player, after which he stayed to sign autographs for other young patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Councillors" title="Councillors">Councillors</a> of <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Knowsley" title="Metropolitan Borough of Knowsley">Knowsley</a> voted to make Gerrard a Freeman of the Borough on 13 December 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> and two weeks later, he was made a Member of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Order of the British Empire</a> by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> in her <a href="/wiki/Orders,_decorations,_and_medals_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Orders, decorations, and medals of the United Kingdom">New Year Honours List</a>, for services to sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> He received an honorary fellowship from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_John_Moores_University" title="Liverpool John Moores University">Liverpool John Moores University</a> on 26 July 2008 as recognition for his contribution to sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 December 2008, Gerrard was taken into custody outside the Lounge Inn in Southport on suspicion of a <a href="/wiki/Grievous_bodily_harm#Section_20" title="Grievous bodily harm">section 20 assault</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assaultarrest_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-assaultarrest-181">[181]</a></sup> He and two others were later charged with assault occasioning actual bodily harm and <a href="/wiki/Affray" title="Affray">affray</a>, relating to an incident which left the bar's <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">disc jockey</a> with a broken tooth and cuts to his forehead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_assault_charge_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_assault_charge-183">[183]</a></sup> The three men were given <a href="/wiki/Bail#Forms" title="Bail">police to court bail</a> and were required to appear at North Sefton <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magistrates%27_Court_(England_and_Wales)" title="Magistrates' Court (England and Wales)">Magistrates' Court</a> on 23 January 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_assault_charge_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_assault_charge-183">[183]</a></sup> where they all pleaded not guilty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-affray_plea_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-affray_plea-184">[184]</a></sup> The case was adjourned until 20 March when the assault charge was dropped but Gerrard was required to attend <a href="/wiki/Crown_Court" title="Crown Court">Liverpool Crown Court</a> to face trial for affray.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chargedropped_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-chargedropped-185">[185]</a></sup> On 3 April, Gerrard pleaded not guilty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>The case went to trial in Liverpool Crown Court. Gerrard's co-defendants pleaded guilty before the trial but Gerrard maintained his innocence. Gerrard admitted hitting Marcus McGee but claimed it was in self-defence and on 24 July, Gerrard was found not guilty by the jury. Following the verdict, Gerrard said he was looking forward to getting back to playing football and putting the experience behind him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, Gerrard appeared in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Will_(2011_film)" title="Will (2011 film)">Will</a></i>, about an orphaned young Liverpool fan who hitch-hikes to the <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">2005 UEFA Champions League Final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> In August 2014, Gerrard participated in the <a href="/wiki/ALS_Association" title="ALS Association">ALS Association</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ice_Bucket_Challenge" title="Ice Bucket Challenge">Ice Bucket Challenge</a> and went on to challenge <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City F.C.</a> winger, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Noone" title="Craig Noone">Craig Noone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> On 9 June 2015, Gerrard was announced as one of <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a>'s pundits on their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> coverage, alongside former team-mate <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_Champions_league_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Champions_league-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his 2015 autobiography, Gerrard has stated that the four best players to have played alongside him are former Liverpool teammates <a href="/wiki/Xabi_Alonso" title="Xabi Alonso">Xabi Alonso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Luis Suárez">Luis Suárez</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> teammate <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span></h3>
<p>Gerrard has had several different sponsorships in his career including current deals with <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar Cars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lucozade" title="Lucozade">Lucozade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> In 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> listed his combined income from salaries, bonuses and off-field earnings at $17.2 million for the previous 12 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> While Gerrard has worn several football boots during his career, he first wore a pair of Nike boots on his Liverpool debut, but soon signed a deal with Adidas in 1998 and has gone on to appear in a number of Adidas commercials with the likes of <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kak%C3%A1" title="Kaká">Kaká</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Gerrard has worn ten versions of the <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Predator" title="Adidas Predator">Adidas Predator</a> boot, with the Accelerator being the first, and throughout his career he has been one of the brand's major boot endorsees. In 2013, Gerrard switched boot silos to the Nitrocharge 1.0 first wearing the boots in the League Cup clash against rivals Manchester United on 25 September 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
<div>Due to a transfer of broadcast rights, the entries for the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_in_English_football" title="2001–02 in English football">2001–02</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_in_English_football" title="2002–03 in English football">2002–03</a> and <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_in_English_football" title="2003–04 in English football">2003–04</a> seasons were decided on <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Premiership_(TV_series)" title="The Premiership (TV series)">The Premiership</a></i>.</div>

</th>
